Jamison Brereton

17 (843)
Various Divinities: Saran╠гyu╠Д (1тАУ2), Pu╠Дsan (3тАУ6), ╠г
Sarasvat─▒ (7тАУ9), the Waters (10, 14), the Waters or Soma (11тАУ13) ╠Д
Deva┼Ыravas Y─Бm─Бyana
14 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except anuс╣гс╣нubh or purast─Бdbr╠еhat─л 13, anuс╣гс╣нubh 14
This hymn consists of a disparate collection of segments, which do not seem to form a coherent whole and which do not always have an obvious connection to the death/funeral context of this cycle of hymns.
The first two enigmatic verses may well be the most discussed of all R╠еgvedic mythological sketches, although this wide-ranging and ongoing discussion has not brought as much clarity as could be desired. The verses provide us with a skeletal three-generation mythological family tree, with a father, the god Tvaс╣гс╣нar, and his daughter, who is identified as both mother of Yama and wife of Vivasvant. All this is fairly clearly set out in the first verse: it opens with a Svayaс╣Гvara (тАЬself-choice marriageтАЭ) invitation issued by the father for his daughter, to which the whole world responds (1ab), and the second half (1cd) appears to summarize the results of that marriageтАФthe husband chosen apparently being Vivasvant, and the child issuing from the marriage apparently being Yama. (It should be noted, though, that the identity of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs daughter [1a] with the mother of Yama [1c] and wife of Vivasvant [1d] is only implicit from context, not expressly stated, and her name is not given in vs. 1.) The only disquieting part of this verse comes with the last word: тАЬshe disappearedтАЭ (nan─Б┼Ыa). This word sets the stage for its companion verse.
The second verse considerably muddies the clean lines of our initial family tree. It turns out that the vanished woman of verse 1 was actually hidden away (2a) by an unnamed set of individualsтАФperhaps the gods, who create and pass off on (the unsuspecting?) Vivasvant a simulacrum of his wife (2b). In the second half of the verse the neat maternal line of 1c is likewise made obscure: someone (the origi
nal woman? the simulacrum?) bears the A┼Ыvins (2c), and she (or the other female) leaves behind (abandons? leaves as a legacy?) two unnamed paired ones (2d). Yama, the son in 1c, is not mentioned by name, but he may lurk as part of the two in 2d (Yama and Yam─л? Yama and Manu?), who could on the other hand be the afore
mentioned A┼Ыvins. Each of these possibilities has had its scholarly champions (and it has in fact also been argued that 2d refers to two pairs, that is four in all). The last word of verse 2 is the feminine name Saraс╣Зy┼л (lit., тАЬhasteningтАЭ), seeming to identify our protagonist, but the name provides little help, and could, in principle, belong to either the original or the duplicate woman.
All in all, the two verses seem deliberately and cleverly designed to mislead and confuse, and in that they have admirably succeeded, beginning with the retellings of the story in the later Vedic tradition and continuing to this day. The myth has also often been invoked in a comparative Indo-European context. (For a recent discus
sion of the history of scholarship and for his own Indo-European interpretation, see Jackson 2006: Part II: esp. 72тАУ93.) This is not the place to produce a full treat ment of the myth behind the verses or its various interpretations; suffice it to say that we are inclined to see the paired two in 2d as Yama and Yam─л, in part because a connection with YamaтАЩs history is the only way to make sense of the inclusion of these verses here.
The relevance of the next set of verses (4тАУ6), to P┼лс╣гan, is considerably clearer. P┼лс╣гan as the good guide and finder of lost livestock makes an excellent psycho pomp, leading the dead along the dangerous path to the next world.
The goddess, and river, Sarasvat─л is addressed in the next three verses (7тАУ9), with a final verse (10) to the Waters in general. Sarasvat─л here seems especially connected with the dead forefathers and the offerings to them at the ritual (esp. vss. 8тАУ9); this may be an early foreshadowing of the later ritual offering of water to the dead, or, as verse 10 suggests, connected with the general purificatory power of waters (see X.9.6тАУ9 earlier in this maс╣Зс╕Нala).

Verses 10тАУ13 concern the тАЬdropтАЭ (draps├б) and are addressed in the 2nd person to Soma, who is never named but clearly identifiable from his characteristic vocabu lary. There is no mention of the forefathers or of anything related to a funeral, and there is no obvious reason why these verses should have been attached to this hymn. Indeed, the final purificatory verse (14) would follow better directly on verse 10.

Jamison Brereton

The next ten hymns (X.10тАУ19) form a Yama cycle, though the subject matter found in the individual hymns is quite various. Yama, the son of Vivasvant, is king of the land of the dead because he was the first mortal to die. Yet he was apparently born immortal (see esp. I.83.5) and chose to become mortal, subject to death, тАЬfor the sake of the gods…and for the sake of offspringтАЭ (X.13.4). The opening hymn in the cycle, the dialogue of Yama and his twin sister Yam─л, on the fraught topic of embarking on incestuous sex in order to produce offspring, addresses YamaтАЩs change of status and his choice, but in a deliberately oblique and misleading fashion, as Yama spurns the sexual advances of his sister, and at the end of their bitter argument there seems little likelihood of children. The last six hymns in this cycle (X.14тАУ19) are collectively known as funeral hymns. The first, X.14, is devoted especially to Yama in his role as king of the realm of the dead, while the others, especially 15тАУ18, concern various aspects of death and the treatment of the deadтАФfor example, the forefathers who preceded us to YamaтАЩs realm in X.15, the cremation fire in X.16, the funeral itself in X.

The intermediate hymns, X.11тАУ13, have less superficially clear connections to the Yama saga, but both X.12 (vss. 6тАУ7) and X.13 (vss. 4тАУ5) make important comments on Yama and on YamaтАЩs choice.

There is also an underlying unifying theme, that of duality and twinned-ness: the absolute disjunction between and the ultimate complementarity and unity of the mortal and the immortal, life and death, men and gods, men and women, heaven and earth, sacred and profane. It is appropriate that the cycle should begin with the dialogue between the primal twins, Yama and Yam─л, whose very names mean тАЬtwinтАЭ and who bridge the gap between mortal and immortal.

English translation:

тАЬTvaс╣гс╣н─Б celebrates the marriage of his daughter; therefore, the whole world is assembled; but themother of Yama, the newly-married wife of the mighty Vivasvat, disappeared.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Deity Saraс╣Зy┼л: The legend:Saraс╣Зy┼л, the daughter of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, was given in marriage to Vivasvat, and had by him Yama and Yam─л.Intimidated by his ardour, she substituted another feminine le, her shadow, Ch─Бy─Б, for herself, and going toUttarakuru, changed herself to a mare. Vivasvat begot Manu by Ch─Бy─Б, when, finding his error, he set off tolook for his wife. Discovering her disguise, he transformed himself to a horse, and had by his wife the twoA┼Ыvins

Jamison Brereton

тАЬTvaс╣гс╣нar is arranging a wedding for his daughterтАЭ: (on hearing) thus, all this world comes together.
The mother of Yama, the wife of great Vivasvant, while being conveyed around (on her wedding journey), went missing.

Griffith

TVASTAR prepares the bridal of his Daughter: all the world hears the tidings and assembles.
But Yama’s Mother, Spouse of great Vivasvan, vanished as she was carried to her dwelling.

рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдВ рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдореЗрддрд╛рдВ рд╕рд░рдгреНрдпреВрдВ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрджреБрддреНрдкрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердореН рдЕрдкрд╛рдЧреВрд╣рдиреН рдЕрдкрдЧреВрд╣рд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рдВрд╡реГрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ ред рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЙрдкрдиреАрддрд╡рдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╕рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛ рд╕рд░рдгреНрдпреВрд╕рджреГрд╢реАрдордиреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡реА рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рддрд╕реНрдореИ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрд╡рддреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЕрджрджреБрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╕рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд┐рдгреА рд╕рд░рдгреНрдпреВрд╕реНрддрджрд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╡рднрд░рддреН ред рд╕реНрд╡реЛрджрд░реЗ рдЧрд░реНрднрднреВрддреМ рдзрд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╡рддреА ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рддрддреН рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдкрддрд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд╢реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ рд╕рдВрднреЛрдЧрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рд░реЗрддрдГ рдкрддрд┐рддрдореН рдЖрд╕реАрддреН рддрджрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдЬрдирдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕реЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рддрдерд╛ рд╕рд░рдгреНрдпреВрдГ рд╕рд░рдгрд╡рддреНрдпреЗрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд┐рдХрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд╛ рдорд┐рдереБрдирд╛ рджреНрд╡реМ рдорд┐рдереБрдиреМ рдпрдордпрдореНрдпреМ рдЕрдЬрд╣рд╛рддреН рддреНрдпрдХреНрддрд╡рддреА ред рдЬрдирд┐рддрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╕рд░рдгреНрдпреВрд░реЗрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд┐рдХрд╛ рдордзреНрдпрдорд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдордзреНрдпрдордордЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдорд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдЪреЛрддреНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╡рддреА рее

English translation:

тАЬThe gods concealing the immortal (Sarс╣Зy┼л) for th esake of mortals and having formed her, gave herto Vivasvat. She bore the two A┼Ыvins when this had happened and then Saraс╣Зy┼л gave birth to two twins.тАЭ

Forthe sake of mortals: maryebhyaс╕е = manuс╣гyebhyas tadutpattyartham, for men, i.e. that men might be born. Jamison Brereton

They hid her away, the immortal, from the mortals. Having made a female of the same appearance, they gave her to Vivasvant.
And she was carrying the A┼Ыvins (in the womb), as it happened, and she left behind the two, the paired ones [=Yama and Yam─л?]тАФSaraс╣Зy┼л.

Griffith

From mortal men they hid the Immortal Lady, made one like her and gave her to Vivasvan.
Saranyu brought to him the Asvin brothers, and then deserted both twinned pairs of children.

Geldner

Sie verbargen die Unsterbliche vor den Sterblichen, machten eine Gleichaussehende und gaben sie dem Vivasvat. Auch ging sie mit den beiden Asvin schwanger, als dies geschah, und sie lie├Я die Zwei, die ein Paar waren, im Stich, die Saranyu.

Grassmann

[Die G├╢tter] verbargen die Unsterbliche vor den Sterblichen; und eine ├дhnlich aussehende bildend gaben sie dieselbe dem Vivasvat, und als dies geschah trug Saranju die beiden A├зvinen als Leibesfrucht und gebar die beiden Zwillinge.

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ-рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдореН-рдЕрдкрд╛рдЧреВрд╣рдиреН) рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдореЗрднреНрдпреЛ Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the discriminating P┼лс╣гan, whose cattle are never lost, the protector of all beings, transfer youhence (to a better world); may he give you to these Pitс╣Ыs; may Agni (give) you to the beneficent gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This andthe following three с╣Ыcas are to be recited at the funeral rites of a man who has been duly initiated, d─лkс╣гita

Jamison Brereton

Let P┼лс╣гan stir you forth from hereтАФthe wise one, whose livestock doesnтАЩt get lost, the herdsman of the world.
He will deliver you to these forefathers; Agni (will deliver you) to the gods who are good to find.

Griffith

Guard of the world, whose cattle ne’er are injured, may Pusan bear thee hence, for he hath knowledge.
May he consign thee to these Fathers’ keeping, and to the gracious Gods let Agni give thee.

Geldner

Pusan soll dich von hier bef├╢rdern, der Kundige, dem kein Vieh verloren geht, der Hirt der Welt. Er ├╝bergebe dich diesen V├дtern, Agni den leichtauffindbaren G├╢ttern.

Grassmann

Dich f├╝hre Puschan fort von hier, der kund’ge, der Hirt der Welt, der nie ein Reich verlieret, Dich m├╢g’ er diesen Ahnen ├╝bergeben, und Agni dich den gabenreichen G├╢ttern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the all-pervading V─Бyu protect you, may P┼лс╣гan (preserve) you, (going) first on the excellentpath (to heaven); may the divine Savit─Б plural ce you, where the virtuous abide, whither they have gone.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аyu =V─Бyu

Jamison Brereton

─Аyu (тАЬLifetimeтАЭ) having a complete lifetime will protect you all around. Let P┼лс╣гan protect you from in front on the path forward.
Where those of good action sit, where they have gone, there let god
Savitar place you.

Griffith

May Ayu, giver of all life, protect thee, and bear thee forward on the distant pathway.
Thither let Savitar the God transport thee, where dwell the pious who have passed-before thee.

Geldner

Ayus m├╢ge dich lebensl├дnglich sch├╝tzen, Pusan soll dich auf der weiten Reise von vorne beh├╝ten. Wo die Frommen ihren Sitz haben, wohin sie gegangen sind, dorthin soll dich Gott Savitri bringen.

Grassmann

Es sch├╝tze dich der Allbeleber Aju, und Puschan vor dir her auf deinem Wege, Wohin die Frommen gingen, wo sie weilen, dahin soll dich Gott Savitar versetzen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬP┼лс╣гan has been born on the best path of paths, on the best path of heaven on the best path ofearth, he goes forward and backward over both (worlds), the assemblies longed for by all, discriminating (themerits of the dead).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

P┼лс╣гan has been born: i.e., manifested in order to conduct men after death to theirdestination, according to their merits; he goes forward: i.e., favourably to the virtuous to show the fruit of goodowrks, backward, i.e., he walks adversely to the wicked; discriminating the merits: i.e., he walks adversely to thewicked

Jamison Brereton

On the forward path of paths was P┼лс╣гan born, on the forward path of heaven, on the forward path of earth.
He wanders back and forth to both the dearest seats, foreknowing.

Griffith

Pusan was born to move on distant pathways, on the road far from earth and far from heaven.
To both most wonted places of assembly he travels and returns with perfect knowledge.

Geldner

In der Ferne der Wege ist Pusan geboren, in der Ferne des Himmels, in der Ferne der Erde. Zu beiden liebsten St├дtten geht er hin und her, des Weges kundig.

Grassmann

Erzeugt ist Puschan auf der Bahn der Pfade auf Himmels Bahn und auf der Bahn der Erde, Zu beiden St├дtten, zu den liebsten Sitzen geht hin er und zur├╝ck, des Weges kundig.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe devout invoke Sarasvat─л; they worship Sarasvat─л at the strewn sacrifice; the virtuous call uponSarasvat─л; may Sarasvat─л bestow blessings upon the donor (of the oblation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sarasvat─л do those seeking the gods invoke, Sarasvat─л when the ceremony is being extended.
Sarasvat─л did those of good action invoke. Sarasvat─л will give a thing of value to the pious.

Griffith

The pious call Sarasvati, they worship Sarasvati while sacrifice proceedeth.
The pious called Sarasvati aforetime. Sarasvati send bliss to him who giveth.

Geldner

Sarasvati rufen die Gottverlangenden an, die Sarasvati, w├дhrend die heilige Handlung vollzogen wird. Die Sarasvati riefen die Frommen, Sarasvati m├╢ge dem Opferspender W├╝nschenswertes geben.

Grassmann

Sarasvati, sie rufen an die Frommen, Sarasvati, wenn sie das Opfer weben, Sarasvati rief einst die Schar der Sel’gen, Sarasvati verleihe Gut dem Opfrer.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDivine Sarasvat─л, who rides in the same chariot with the Pitс╣Ыs, and delighted (along with them) by the(sacrificial) viands, seated on the sacred grass gratified (by our offering, and grant us wholesome food. worshippers at this sacrifice a portion of food fit for thousands, and increase of riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Sarasvat─л, you who drove on the same chariot with the forefathers, becoming exhilarated at the svadh─Б(-calls), o goddessтАФ
having taken your seat here on this ritual grass, bring yourself to
exhilaration. Provide us refreshments that bring no disease.

Griffith

Sarasvati, who camest with the Fathers, with them rejoicing thee in our oblations,
Seated upon this sacred grass be joyful, and give us strengthening food that brings no sickness.

Grassmann

Sarasvati, die du auf gleichem Wagen dich mit den V├дtern gern berauschend, nahtest, Setz heute dich auf diese Streu, berausch dich, gesunde Tr├дnke spende uns, o G├╢ttin.

Jamison Brereton

Sarasvat─л, whom the forefathers invoke, as they arrive at the sacrifice in the southтАФ
provide here a portion of refreshment worth thousands and thriving of wealth among the sacrificers.

Griffith

Thou, called on as Sarasvati by Fathers who come right forward to our solemn service,
Give food and wealth to present sacrificers, a portion, worth a thousand, of refreshment.

Geldner

Sarasvati, die die V├дter anrufen, von rechts zum Opfer antretend, gib du dabei den tausendwertigen Teil der Opferspende, gib den Opfernden Zunahme des Reichtums!

Grassmann

Sarasvati, die unsre Ahnen rufen, die rechter Hand zum Opfer jetzt erscheinen, Gib tausendfachen Antheil an der Labung und Reichthums Mehrung denen, die dir opfern.

Elizarenkova

рдорд╛рддрд░рдГ рдЬрдЧрддреЛ рдорд╛рддреГрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ рдЖрдкрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╢реБрдиреНрдзрдпрдиреНрддреБ рдкреНрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрди рд╢реЛрдзрдпрдиреНрддреБред рддрдерд╛ рдШреГрддрдкреНрд╡рдГред рдШреГрддрдореБрджрдХрдореН ред рддреЗрдирд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдкреБрдирдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ ред рддрд╛рд╕реНрддрдереЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рдЖрдкрдГред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдШреГрддрдкреНрд╡рдГ ред рдШреГрддрдВ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддреЗрди рдкреБрдирдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдВ– рдШреГрддреЗрди рдиреЛ рдШреГрддрдкреНрд╡рдГ рдкреБрдирдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡реИ рд╕реБрдкреВрддрдВ рдпрджреНрдШреГрддреЗрди рдкреВрдпрддреЗ’ (рд╢. рдмреНрд░рд╛. рей.рез.реи.резрез ) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрд╛ рдЖрдкрдГ рдШреГрддреЗрди рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгреЛрджрдХреЗрди рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкреБрдирдиреНрддреБ ред рд╣рд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рджреЗрд╡реАрдГ рджреЗрд╡реНрдпреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛ рдЖрдкрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рд░рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рдЧрдордпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдкрдирдпрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЖрднреНрдпрдГ рдЕрджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдЖ рдкреВрддрдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрди рд╢реБрджреНрдзрдГ рд╕рдиреН рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд╣рдореН рдЙрддреН рдПрдорд┐ рдЙрджреНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдорд┐ ред рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдореАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рее реирек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the maternal waters, purify us; may the shedders of water purify us with the effusion; for thedivine (waters) bear away all sin; I come away from them purified (to heaven).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Shedders of wateс╣Ы..with effusioс╣Еghс╣Ыtena no ghс╣Ыtapvaс╕е punantu: waters which purify others by water;

Ghс╣Ыta = effused water;

Ghс╣Ыtapvaс╕е =divinities presiding over effused water; or, ghс╣Ыta = oiled butter (Yajus. 4.2);

Udemi = I go to heaven (┼ЪatapathaBr─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.1.2.11)

Jamison Brereton

Let the waters, the mothers cleanse us; let them, ghee-pure, purify us with their ghee,
for the goddesses carry forth every defilement. I rise up from them
gleaming, purified.

Griffith

The Mother Floods shall make us bright and shining, cleansers of holy oil, with oil shall cleanse us:
For, Goddesses, they bear off all defilement: I, rise up from them purified and brightened.

Geldner

Die m├╝tterlichen Gew├дsser sollen uns reinigen, sie sollen uns mit Schmalz l├дutern, die wie Schmalz Gel├дuterten, denn alles Unreine f├╝hren die G├╢ttinnen fort, aus ihnen komme ich rein und lauter heraus.

Grassmann

Die Gew├дsser, die M├╝tter, m├╢gen uns reinigen, die Butter l├дuternden m├╢gen uns mit Butter l├дutern; denn sie, die G├╢ttinnen, f├╝hren jede Unreinigkeit hinweg; aus ihnen gehe ich rein gekl├дrt hervor.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Soma has risen to the earthly and heavenly (worlds), both this visible world, and that which(existed) before (it); I offer that Soma flowing through the common region (of heaven and earth) after the sacrifice(offered by the) seven (officiating priests).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Drapsam = a name of the Sun (┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa: 8.4.1.20);

Hotr─Бс╕е = ditaс╕е, which are seven: zenith, nadir, centre and four cardinal points

Jamison Brereton

The drop spurted through the first days, both through this womb here and the former one.
I offer the drop circling around through the same womb, according to the seven priestly functions.

Griffith

Through days of earliest date the Drop descended on this place and on that which was before it.
I offer up, throughout the seven oblations, the Drop which still to one same place is moving.

Geldner

Der Tropfen fiel daneben an den ersten Tagen, in diesen Scho├Я und in den, der es vorher war. Den Tropfen, der dem gemeinsamen Scho├Яe zustrebt, den opfere ich f├╝r jedes der sieben Priester├дmter.

Grassmann

Der Tropfen ist wie in den ersten Tagen herabgefallen in diesen Schooss, und in den der fr├╝her war; die Tropfen, die nach dem gleichen Schoosse gemeinsam wandern, giesse ich aus gem├дss den [├╝blichen] sieben Opferg├╝ssen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSoma, which escapes (from the hide), your filaments which let fall from the hands (of the priestescape) from the vicinity of the plural nks (of the press), or (from the hand) of the Adhvaryu, or from the filter; I offer itall with my mind (to Agni) with the word vaс╣гat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your drop that spurts and your plant that is set in motion by the arms, from the lap of the Holy Place,
or from the Adhvaryu or from the filter, that one of yours I offer with my mind when the vaс╣гaс╣н-cry is made.

Griffith

The Drop that falls, thy stalk which arms have shaken, which from the bosom of the press hath fallen,
Or from the Adhvaryu’s purifying filter, I offer thee with heart and cry of Vasat!

Geldner

Welcher Tropfen von dir daneben f├дllt, welche Stengel den Armen entfallen, aus dem Scho├Яe der Dhisana oder aus der Hand des Adhvaryu oder von der Seihe, den opfere ich dir im Geiste mit Vasatrufe gesegnet.

Grassmann

Dein Tropfen, welcher herabf├дllt, dein von den Armen in Bewegung gesetzter Saft, der aus dem Schoosse der Schale herabf├дllt, sei es von dem Opferpriester her oder aus der Seihe, den giesse ich mit Verstand aus, den Opferruf sprechend. [Das Versmass verlangt vaс╣гaс╣нk┼Хt statt v├бс╣гaс╣нkс╣Щtam].

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Waters)! the plural nts flourish by means of water my prayer is effectual through water; the essence ofwater is vigorous through water; purify me with it.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Payasvat = having water; or, s─Бravat, having pith or vigour;being vigorous b\y means of water in the shape of rain

Jamison Brereton

Full of milk are the plants, full of milk my little speech.
Full of milk indeed is the milk of the waters. With it cleanse me
altogether.

Griffith

The plants of earth are rich in milk, and rich in milk is this my speech;
And rich in milk the essence of the Waters: make me pure therewith.

Geldner

Saftreich sind die Pflanzen, saftreich ist mein Wort; saftreich ist des Wassers Saft, mit dem zusammen reinigt mich!

Grassmann

Nahrungsreich sind die Kr├дuter, nahrungsreich ist mein Lied, nahrungsreich auch ist der Saft der Gew├дsser, durch den reiniget mich allesammt.

Elizarenkova
